Really really good! Nice to had a new place to go on this end of town! The food was excellent and the service was outstanding. I was happy to see the prices were reasonable- hope they stay that way. For a small place, it was busy and didn't seem crowded and loud. I remember the owner from another popular Japanese place in town and he knows what he's doing! Nicely decorated, clean and very well staffed. Can't wait to go back and try something new! I went with some old fav's since my date was buying and she didn't like going out on a limb and trying anything new. Nice place!<//review>

It's a small size family owned restaurant. The owner was formerly a sushi chef at Tokyo Garden. The sushi was great. We ordered California rolls, Shrimp Tempura rolls, Mountain Dew roll, Jasmine rolls, a Philly roll, and Unagi nigiri. The wait was pretty long, but overall the customer service and food was great. It would have been nice if we had been informed of the wait time, however, the host and hostess were both very nice and apologizing for the wait. Will be back in the future.< /text>

<Rating>3<//Rating><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< name>
Rich Perez< /name>
<GmapID>0x54d2eb0e8ee16325:0xeae8a70e88edbbc2</GmapID>< Review>
The food was good, it certainly wasn't bad, but, being from the Bay Area, when you compare, there really isn't any.

I suppose being up in the North State, having sushi, you have to expect that.

My suggestions.

Just having fish on rice dosen't make it sushi. Take a bit more time on appearance. It's part of enjoying great Japanese food.

Also, I know its probably hard to get real fresh fish, but it's a must. Must have fresh garnish too. It's a must. There was no miso soup with dinner, which is a must, or at least offer.

Again, spoiled, from the Bay, but..no buts.
Gotta have it.

3 stars for being our first experience in Redding.

Thanks you!</Review>

<Text>This place doesn't get enough love for the food it serves - authentic Northern Chinese dishes. For the uninitiated, all those flower pepper / ginger / spicy type dishes you see in TV shows about China is the cuisine they serve here. Most of the Chinese food you get in mixed restaurants (let's say that also serve Vietnamese, Korean or Thai) don't serve the same type of food you would get at a place like this.

Although the food is tasty, the prices are a bit high. Also the ambient decor of the restaurant is a little disheveled looking. Factor in horrible parking during weekends and busy lunch hours, and it's a restaurant you really have to be in the mood for to make the trip if you're not a local. They also do take-out if you rather eat at home, but you have to know what to order (it's a traditional menu style restaurant - no bright signs or anything)< /Text>< gmap_id>

<Rating>3<//Rating>< review>
Unfortunately, some promises made during the sales process fall well short and management is disorganized and, at times, unprofessional. Price is on par with the higher end companies and systems. Expect to pay about $18k for a 5 ton AC and heating system using existing ducts, including permits. The biggest issue that I had was the emphasis on certain guarantees and policies made during the sales process. One item singled out by the salesman was the "Customer Respect" clause that states technicians will not use tobacco products while on property. I guess smoking in my driveway was an exception? The next was the "Property Protection Guarantee" that states "Damaged property will be replaced or repaired."  They had to cut a larger hole in the attic to get the new unit in -- no problem -- totally understandable.  But they don't have any drywall experts on staff, so they sent out a contractor who, in front of me, discussed how he doesn't have the right parts to install bull-nosed edges.  So he proceeded to install right-angle edging on two sides, butted up against my bull-nosed edges on the two adjacent sides (the whole house has bull-nosed corners on every wall and facet). For 5 months, I continued to tell them that it was wrong and withheld final payment waiting for them to fix it. Despite telling the sales person 3 times, and the backoffice another 2 or 3 times.  It wasn't until some accountant saw the small amount due that we finally agreed that I'd just hire my own contractor to fix it -- that was 5 months after installation! And  regardless of the bull-nose issue, their drywall  sub-contractor failed to match the paint, did a horrible job to where you could see the flashing he installed (metal) and copped an attitude when he didn't like the answer to his question about my satisfaction.  The final straw that drove me to share my experience was the "free" maintenance included in my contract. They called about a month ago and told me that I'm due for maintenance and they'll come out.  Well today, the morning that they were supposed to come out, they called and canceled.  I took time off of work to stay home for this!  Their excuse? "We like to perform maintenance 1 year after installation". Ummm.. YOU CALLED ME!   Whatever. Give me my two free maintenances, honor your warranty and we can agree that any other business will go to competitors. Don't point out your "cool differentiating guarantees" in your contract if you can't live up to them. Honestly had that not been such a big part of the sales pitch, I probably wouldn't have sweated the relatively minor infractions here -- I would have just chalked it up to being a mediocre contractor. Oh well...< /review>

Believe it or not, I read all 56 reviews to learn what customers thought of their experience. with Air Tech  In researching heat pumps, most authors on the web stressed the importance of a quality installation as many of the unit manufacturers on the market produce reliable units for sale in the high end, middle range, and budget sectors.  Air Tech consistently was praised for their quality installations.  We left an emergency email on their website and they called us the next morning. They weren‚Äôt the lowest bid acquired, however; because of a courteous and informational visit with Randy Anderson who listened to what I specifically wanted and then assured me they could deliver as desired, we agreed to hire AirTech for our HVAC overhaul and energy efficiency work.

Five minutes after the installation crew arrived, they started instructing my wife that they could not install the HVAC system as desired. They put on their protective booties in the house but left them outside blowing around the property upon leaving.  Debris was left indiscriminately and we suffered a flat tire because of nails left on the driveway. Additionally, the crew broke the house water line four times during installation.

They returned several times over a five-month period and during the hottest period of the year, and the first time operating the new AC unit, it just blew hot air. We contacted AirTech, as this was not acceptable and were scheduled for service four days out. The first service technician found the transport-packaging fan strapping still attached to the condenser unit.

To date, five months after commencement of the job, the work is still not complete per the contract but rest assured the company‚Äôs management does not care about the contract or customer service they portray on their webpage. I assure you, they will not do everything in their power to ensure you are satisfied with their work, as advertised.
